commit 38d5c7117a6ac7bfd2e49b44c5e0756cf575d249
Author: Steaphan Greene <steaphan@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Dec 7 13:51:16 2022 -0800

    Optimize dSR()
    
    Profiling Run Method:
      make -j clean
      make -j
      ./tests/tests -d yes '[Dice]'
      ./tests/tests -d yes '[Dice]'
      ./tests/tests -d yes '[Dice]'
    <Take Best>
    
    Results:
    
    Original reroller (ok):
      0.110 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Look-Up Table (awful, no!):
      6.306 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical (better, yes):
      0.102 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical, Non-Recursive Hack (better, yes):
      0.097 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical, Non-Recursive (better, yes):
      0.072 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical, Unrolled To 198 (worse, no):
      0.099 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical, Unrolled To 90 (worse, no):
      0.099 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical, Unrolled To 54 (worse, no):
      0.101 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical, Unrolled To 36 (worse, no):
      0.97 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical, Manually Inlined (not better, no):
      0.072 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    3-1 Merged Mathematical, Clarified (not worse, yes):
      0.070 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    5-1 Merged Mathematical, Clarified (better, yes):
      0.063 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    5-1 Merged Mathematical, Flattened to 30 (worse, no):
      0.093 s: SR Dice Rolls
    
    Winner: 5-1 Merged Mathematical, Clarified
    
    This uses a single call to the pseudorandom generator to get a number in a
    range sufficient to fairly represent the possible results of 5 separate dice,
    then converts this value into the result had up to those 5 dice been rolled
    SR-style.  When a roll exceeds 30 (max of 5 dice), then it does this again,
    but for all results less than 30 (almost all) it only needs to do this once.

commit d6a46433a2daa2229451fdffa098247abbd859d4
Author: Steaphan Greene <steaphan@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 3 07:32:45 2022 -0800

    Add script to undo char8_t conversion, for testing std::format.
    
    Unfortunately, std::format is epic broken in the C++20 standard.
    I can't use it at all, without applying this massive codemod.
    
    I don't plan to apply this change, only to use it for testing.
    The C++20 standard forces me to choose between using these fast
    char8_t strings, or using std::format.  I choose fast.
    
    Apparently, because the char8_t std::basic_string is the u8string,
    and because that's supposed to hold UTF8 strings, they were afraid
    of supporting it in format.  So, even though I only use char8_t to
    hold ascii, I can't use std::format at all, and need to stick with
    fmt::format... probably for years (maybe forever).
    
    No, char8_t can't actually hold any UTF8 character, it still only
    holds a single byte.  So, why using this type in my strings forces
    the string type to be considered to be UTF8 is quite befuddling.
    
    So, meanwhile, I'll use this script to occasionally check in with
    std::format, in the hopes of one day getting fully working standard
    C++ formatted text input/output support.

commit 07ccdbf20a1b05645c267254d78019fe752c60b8
Author: Steaphan Greene <steaphan@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Nov 17 20:15:33 2019 -0800

    TBA data file whitespace cleanups.
    
    This just converts the few DOS text files still in here to standard text files (line-endings),
    removes all the trailing spaces on lines, removes all the trailing blank lines, and replaces
    all the tabs (except in .zon files, where they seem to be common) with expanded spaces.
    
    It's easy to confirm this is actually a non-change, except for whitespace:
    * `git show -w` shows this commit as only removing 8 trailing blank lines.
    
    This should make no difference to tbaMUD itself, but it will make working on these files,
    especially with scripts and automated tools, much easier.
    
    This is the base change for a set of other changes I will put up once/if this merges,
    without this, the others are just too complicated to wrangle.

commit ee09356e2b96ac90a19132b8ee13f1a50fce95bf
Author: Steaphan Greene <steaphan@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Nov 17 15:39:35 2019 -0800

    Fix a few apparent TBA world consistency errors.
    
    These are mostly cases of confusion between the "on the body"
    and "about the body" slots (5 and 12).
    
    But, there are also some that seem to just be misconfigured,
    like non-weapons being wielded, worn items being unwearable,
    weapons being worn instead of wielded, and items being worn
    instead of held.
    
    I avoided the cases where it was clear this was done intentionally,
    like all the cases where the second neck was used for the missing
    face slot (masks, etc).
    
    The ones fixed here all seem to really be (minor) bugs.
